Ma Zhanshan to Return to China Soon and Come to Shanghai 153

Deputy Commander Xu Jingde has Arrived to Await Him

Xu Discussed the Bitter Battle Against Japan in Heilongjiang Province

The Central News Agency reports that since General Ma Zhanshan left Heilongjiang for Russia, all of General Ma's troops have been under the command of Xu Jingde, Deputy Commander of Heilongjiang Province. Xu recently heard that General Ma will return to China soon, so he came to Shanghai via Heilongjiang to await General Ma's arrival before returning to his defense area to plan the recovery of the lost territory. The Central News Agency reporter visited Xu at his residence yesterday and asked about the recent situation in Heilongjiang Province. He was pleased to be interviewed and answered in detail as follows.

Experience of Bitter Battles 154

According to Xu, I am from the Northeast and belong to the military. Since the September 18th Incident, Chairman Ma Zhanshan took charge of the Heilongjiang government and engaged in anti-Japanese work. I was involved in the Jiangqiao and Daxing battles. On the 4th of last month, Chairman Ma went to Heihe to re-establish the provincial government. Not long after, he personally led troops. At that time, he ordered me to be the commander of the Heihe garrison and acting deputy commander, staying behind to coordinate all routes. For several months, along the upper and lower reaches of Heihe, for defense, China advanced and occupied Nenjiang to the south to spy on Nehe, and advanced and occupied Luobei to the east to plot Suibin. The enemy repeatedly attacked the two routes in the middle but were repelled. Suibin, the fundamental place, was once recovered. The defense was consolidated. However, Heihe is known to be barren, and the people's food and various materials are extremely lacking. Bullets, the only necessary military item, have no source. Troops and volunteers from all routes requested pay and ammunition, causing me to feel exhausted. It took great effort to cope for several months, and Heihe became increasingly empty. At this time, Chairman Ma was stationed in Nehe, planning to attack the Harbin station, and urged the Su and Zhang armies in Hailar and Zhalantun to take action. He also went to discuss strategy, hoping to make unified progress and restore the provincial capital. Unexpectedly, the situation changed after Chairman Ma arrived in Zhalantun. Because he was isolated and unable to return, Chairman Ma withdrew into Russian territory via Manchuria, hoping to return to China and plan a major campaign.

Waiting for an Opportunity to Act 155

However, after resolving the Hailar-Manzhouli issue, the enemy concentrated its forces to attack Heihe. I originally planned to concentrate the troops and defend the Xing'an Mountains, fighting the violent Japanese to the death. However, the pay and ammunition were too scarce. Although I had the determination to die, I had no means to fight the enemy. As a last resort, I handed over the various units under my command to Chief of Staff Wang and the brigade commanders to maintain order and secretly gave them instructions to temporarily lie dormant in the various counties, totaling 16,000 people. I instructed them to wait for an opportunity to act. In addition, there were commander Pu Bingshan's army, Cai Hongyou's army, Nan Tingfang's army, Zhang Xishi's unit, and Xu Haiting's unit, totaling 50,000 to 60,000 people, who were all out of ammunition and food, thinly clothed, and unable to fight. They were lying dormant in various counties. Army Commander Xu Haiting, due to his old age, fought bitterly in the Laha station and Nehe area for several days. His arm was affected by rheumatism and he has already come to Shanghai for medical treatment. Army Commander Zhang Xishi is said to have also arrived in Beiping, requesting assistance.

Ma's Impending Arrival in Shanghai 156

I have heard that Chairman Ma [Likely refers to a prominent figure named Ma, potentially relating to political or military leadership] is soon to arrive in Shanghai. He will discuss a comprehensive plan for recovering lost territories with the central government and military authorities in North China. He disguised himself and changed his name, detouring through Vladivostok to Shanghai. He is currently suffering from heart disease due to the overwhelming stimulation. He intends to rest and recuperate in Shanghai for a while. After Chairman Ma returns to the country, he will follow him again, jointly deliberating on measures to save the situation. However, I, as a soldier, bear heavy military responsibilities. I failed to defend even a small corner of pure land on the border, leading to the retreat of the Heilongjiang provincial government. I am filled with shame. This time, I left with tears and intense grief. Therefore, I am unwilling to express myself much to the press. Since you have inquired, I must briefly recount my experiences. Chairman Ma has already left Vawkas. He should arrive in Shanghai in the shortest possible time.

The Shanghai East Refusal to Cut-Off Water Association Petitioned the Municipal Council Yesterday 162

Commissioner He Dekui Received Them, but Talks Were Unfruitful

The Municipal Council Board Meeting Will Discuss It Tomorrow

The Shanghai East Refusal to Cut-Off Water Joint Committee dispatched six representatives yesterday morning to submit a petition to the Municipal Council, requesting it to promptly order the water company to resume water supply immediately to protect people's lives. The details of the petition are as follows:

Petition Situation: The petition representatives of the association petitioned the Municipal Council authorities at approximately 10:00 AM yesterday. Commissioner He Dekui received them. The representatives described the suffering after the water cut-off and requested the water company to hand over water meters and resume water supply immediately. The response was that discussions are currently underway among all parties, and significant progress has been made. After the matter is submitted to the board meeting on Wednesday, a resolution will be made. The representatives felt that such statements had already appeared in the newspapers and requested the director-general to respond personally. Since the director-general was unavailable, they dispersed without any results.

Petition: Respectfully submitted. It is found that the British-owned Shanghai Waterworks Company has been using water cut-offs in the eastern districts of Shanghai to coerce the collection of a huge sum of water fees calculated according to the water meter. As a result, residents have no water to cook with and their lives are in imminent danger. This association's responsibility is related, so Qiu Jialiang, Chen Baoshi, Chen Xintian, Qu Qinghua, Wang Yaozeng, and Gao Yiqun have been specially sent to visit the director-general to present the difficult situation in person. We earnestly request that the water company be ordered to restore the water supply immediately and reject the household water meter installation system to save people's livelihoods. We would be eternally grateful.

Company Statement: According to reliable sources, after mediation on the water fees by relevant parties, the water company stated that there must be restrictions on residents' water use, with a limit of seven gallons per person per day. For example, in each building, calculated with sixteen people, the monthly water usage needs 3360 gallons. Calculated at six jiao and four fen per 1,000 gallons, the total is two yuan and eight fen. If the above quota is exceeded, fees will be charged as usual. It is now being strongly argued by relevant parties that at least 23 gallons per person per day must be supplied (because there are also restrictions in Europe and the United States with a limit of 23 gallons per person per day). The water fee is calculated as one-tenth of the rent. Negotiations are currently underway, and if there are results, they will be submitted to the Municipal Council board meeting tomorrow (Wednesday) for discussion and decision.

Seeking Equal Treatment: The Zhoujia Pai Road and Shuncheng Li on Yangshupu Road in eastern Shanghai have been very desolate since the January 28th Incident. In light of the suffering of businessmen, the landlords have automatically reduced rents. The monthly rent for each store in that area is only 30 yuan, and since June of last year, it has been reduced by 20%. Therefore, the relationship between landlords and tenants is very harmonious. The housing in Shuncheng Li belongs to the same landlord, but the treatment is different. This has caused dissatisfaction among the tenants. They have organized an autonomous association to request that the landlord treat everyone equally and reduce rents by 20%. However, the landlord has procrastinated until now and has not fulfilled this request. Suffering again from the pain of the water cut-off, an autonomous association meeting was convened the day before yesterday and resolved to deposit the most recent rent due into the Trust Department of the Bank of China to promote the landlord's awareness and achieve the goal of rent reduction.

Zheng Xitang's Fatal Record 163

The Coffin Will Be Sealed Tomorrow at the China Funeral Parlor

Zheng Xitang, a giant in the aviation industry, was kidnapped by local bandits at the Xintai Wharf in the South City on the afternoon of the eleventh of last month. He struggled to escape but was shot in the back of the head, and his Russian bodyguard, Sadif, was killed. Zheng Jin died in the hospital from illness. After Zheng was injured, he was taken by car to Shanghai Hospital and then to the Red Cross Hospital in Hongkou, where he was placed in Room 15. Western doctors attempted to remove the bone fragments and shrapnel from the edge of his skull and gave him pain-relieving medicine. His condition improved, and his appetite was reduced, and he could eat milk and thin porridge. However, his bowel movements were blocked, requiring a machine to extract them. After two weeks, the wound became inflamed again, and his old kidney problems were triggered, causing his fever to increase daily. The doctors were helpless. Finally, his friend Lu Bohong (a director of the Red Cross Hospital) accompanied a well-known Western doctor to the hospital to examine his condition and attempt to save him. Upon examination, although Zheng's brain had not been damaged by the bullet, fragments of Zheng's hair had become embedded in his brain, making it impossible to remove them. The hair fragments caused inflammation in the brain, making him difficult to save. He passed away at 11:40 PM on the fifth night. His body was taken by car to the China Funeral Parlor at 670 Haig Road. The coffin will be sealed at 2:00 PM on the eighth (tomorrow). Zheng was 41 years old and had four sons and two daughters. The eldest son, Yinian, has entered the business world and inherited his father's business. Zheng had a wide circle of friends. While he was in the hospital, friends in Shanghai came to visit, and his secretary, Xu Wanli, and others handled the reception. There will certainly be many mourners at the sealing of the coffin tomorrow.

The Butler's Dream of Wealth 164

Stealing His Master's Diamond Ring and Cash

Traveling to Tiger Hill and Returning to Shanghai

Enjoying Harlots All Day at the Hotel

Being Arrested One Day, Joy Turns to Sorrow

Zhang Acai, from Ningbo, is 30 years old. He has been working as a butler for a Frenchman named Maitai (transliteration) at No. 603 Haig Road, French Concession. From the 3rd to the 27th of last month, he successively stole five diamond rings worth 16,500 francs and 851 yuan in cash from his master's room. After absconding in private, the victim discovered the theft and reported it to the police for arrest. After Zhang committed the theft, he and his friend Chen Aming (24 years old) each had a stylish pair of jodhpurs made, as well as new robes and clothing. Each wearing a diamond ring, they acted like wealthy young men, traveling to Suzhou together. They stayed at a hotel at night, touring scenic spots such as Tiger Hill during the day. One day, they happened to pass in front of a photography studio on Xin Xian Qian Street, where they saw a woman idly gazing outside. Zhang and others immediately went forward to tease her. (According to reports, the woman's surname is Liu, named Zhifen, 18 years old, and is a foster daughter-in-law of the photography studio.) The woman thought Zhang and others were handsome young men, each wearing dazzling diamond rings, mistaking them for wealthy young masters. She was moved, so she did not refuse and even struck up a conversation with them. She was soon lured to the hotel and slept with them for several nights. Later, they encountered a prostitute named Wang Xiuying at the same place. After talking, they felt like they had met late in life. Then, on the 3rd of this month, Zhang and others brought Wang Xiuying and Liu Zhifen to Shanghai, staying in Room 376 of the Dongfang Hotel on Xizang Road. Soon after, they became acquainted with Wang Fengbao, a prostitute at No. 280 Huile Li, and gave each prostitute a diamond ring. The prostitutes were overjoyed to have met such generous customers, and they accompanied them all day, never leaving their side. The sound of laughter reached outside. Unexpectedly, sadness came from within. The matter was discovered by detectives Kang Guangfu and Bao Tan Gu Mingzhou of the French police. They rushed to the Dongfang Hotel the day before yesterday and arrested all the above people, seizing the original stolen diamond rings and other items. Yesterday, they were escorted to the Second Special Court Criminal Division II. First, the police lawyer Gu Shouxi explained the case, stating that the case still needs to be investigated and requesting a rescheduling of the hearing. Judge Zhang Renkan questioned each defendant and then ordered Zhang and Chen to be returned to custody. Wang Fengbao was released on bail. The two women, Wang Xiuying and Liu Zhifen, were sent by the police to the Suzhou Public Security Bureau for disposition. The case was rescheduled for the 13th.

Oversupply of Doctors in Shanghai 165

Income Does Not Cover Expenses, and Living is Difficult

According to Zhu Dianxuan, president of the Rural Medical Improvement Society, the society recently conducted a survey of doctors in Shanghai and discovered the alarming oversupply of doctors in the city. There are 413 Western doctors and 2018 Chinese medicine doctors (not including unlicensed doctors). More than 80% of them have incomes that do not cover their expenses, and living is very difficult. As a result, various unethical behaviors arise. In fact, there is not a nationwide oversupply of doctors. Currently, there are approximately 400,000 doctors in China, which means there is one doctor for every 1,000 people, similar to the ratio in England. Therefore, it has not reached a truly excessive level. The reason is that in recent years, the rural economy has collapsed, and farmers' lives are mostly unable to support themselves. When they are sick, they often have no ability to seek medical treatment, relying on the natural changes of the disease. As a result, rural doctors are forced by life to run to the cities. The increase in the number of Chinese medicine doctors in Shanghai in the past three years alone shows the tendency of doctors to move to the cities. There were 436 more in 1920, 375 more in 1921, and 605 more in 1922 (last year). This trend is enough to further exacerbate the rural medical famine, which is the biggest crisis for the nation's future. Therefore, the mutual academic attacks in recent years between the Chinese and Western medical communities are meaningless. The fundamental problem is the high national population mortality rate and how to lower it, how to provide relief to the more than 20 million sick and suffering patients, and how to ensure the livelihoods of the majority of unemployed doctors. These are all urgent problems that the medical community itself needs to solve and are the only way to actively save the country.

Yesterday's Meeting of the United Association for the Murder of Chinese by Vietnamese Police, Resolving to Petition the Municipal Government Tomorrow and Requesting Assistance from Du Yuesheng in Negotiations 166

The case of the Vietnamese police officer of French Concession Police Station No. 427 shooting and killing a Chinese person has aroused public outrage from all sectors. Various organizations have formed a United Association for Aiding the Victims, appointing responsible personnel to conduct negotiations. The association held its first meeting yesterday, resolving several important matters. The details are recorded as follows:

Collective Discussion of Response: Yesterday afternoon at 3 PM, the United Association for Aiding the Victims of the French Concession Tragedy, convened its first committee meeting at the fourth floor of the Ningbo Native Place Association. Attendees included Zheng Zhengqiu, Qu Zhenhua, Cao Zhigong, Jiang Junyi, Zheng Ziliang, Dong Xinfang, Gu Wensheng, Wu Mai, and over ten others. Chairman Zheng Zhengqiu reported on the previous day's contact with Du's residence and read aloud the draft letter to Du Yuesheng requesting assistance in negotiations. Then, the meeting commenced with discussions on: (1) The matter of publicly appointing persons responsible for drafting various letters and telegrams. It was resolved to appoint Cao Zhigong and Zhang Shenzhi as the responsible persons. (2) The matter of publicly appointing representatives to the Municipal Government to request serious negotiations. It was resolved to appoint Zheng Zhengqiu, Jiang Junyi, Zhang Shenzhi, Qu Zhenhua, Ye Xianggao, and five others to go. (3) The matter of researching and estimating the losses of the bereaved families. It was resolved to publicly appoint six lawyers, Wu Kaisheng, Tu Zhenhu, Cai Xiaobai, Guo Qimin, Dai Jinghuai, and Qu Shao Yi, to conduct research. In addition to sending letters, each fellow-villagers association will separately contact the respective lawyers to investigate the situation of the families of the victims tomorrow morning. At 5 PM, they will meet at the Ningbo Native Place Association to discuss compensation methods, draft them in writing, and leave them to representative Zhang Shenzhi to take to the Municipal Government. (4) It was decided to hold the second committee meeting at 5 PM on Wednesday, at the same address at the Ningbo Native Place Association. The meeting adjourned.

Letter to Du Yuesheng: The Association sent a letter yesterday to Du Yuesheng, Chairman of the Chinese Ratepayers Association of the French Concession, stating: "Respected Sir, On the 25th of last month, the case of the Vietnamese police officer of French Concession Police Station No. 427 indiscriminately shooting and killing multiple people has caused deep indignation among the citizens. Not only should the victims be assisted, but it also concerns the safety of all citizens in the concession thereafter. Various organizations in this city especially convened a meeting yesterday at the Ningbo Native Place Association to discuss response measures. It was resolved to organize the Shanghai United Association for Aiding the Victims of the French Concession Tragedy to manage the proceedings. The demands are as follows: (1) In accordance with Chinese law, the murderer must be severely punished and executed locally. (2) Generous compensation should be given to the deceased and medical treatment provided to the injured. (3) Assurance must be given that the same unfortunate incident will not occur again in the future. (4) The police station must show respect. (5) Vietnamese police officers should be replaced to avoid further incidents caused by language barriers and ignorance of local customs. (6) The practice of two people riding in one vehicle should be abolished, and reference should be made to the methods used in the Chinese and Public Concessions. Those who are mistakenly arrested should be handled flexibly, considering the circumstances. Zheng Zhengqiu, Jiang Junyi, Zhang Shenzhi, Tu Zhenhu, Cao Zhigong, Qu Zhenhua, Tong Lizhang, and others have been nominated as representatives to visit your office to request that you uphold justice and actively negotiate. Your immediate attention to this matter is urgently requested. It is hoped that you will provide assistance in negotiations, and actively proceed to uphold justice and ensure protection. This would be greatly appreciated."

The Municipal Council Replied to Two Important Letters from the Ratepayers Association Yesterday 168

The Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers Association received two reply letters from the Public Concession Municipal Council yesterday. Excerpts are recorded below:

Discussion of Tap Water: The Ratepayers Association previously received a letter from the Shanghai Citizens Federation stating that the water bills had increased due to the use of meters for tap water within the concession, and suggested solutions. They forwarded the letter to the Municipal Council for handling. The council replied yesterday, stating, "Your esteemed letter of February 20 is acknowledged. Regarding the water price issue, this council is currently consulting with the Real Estate Association and the Tenant Federation. The opinions expressed by the two associations have been taken into consideration in the hope of reaching a satisfactory solution as soon as possible. This letter is for your information." After receiving the letter, the association forwarded it to the City Federation for their information.

Robbery of Watch Store: The Ratepayers Association previously received a letter from the Shanghai Watch Industry Association regarding the robbery of watch stores and forwarded it to the Public Concession Municipal Council for handling. The council replied yesterday, stating, "Your esteemed letter of February 20 is acknowledged, regarding the letter from the Shanghai Watch Industry Association about the robbery of watch stores. Upon investigation of the Police Department's records, it is found that the claim of robbers especially targeting watch stores in recent years is not supported by facts. From July 1 of last year to February 20 of this year, only two cases occurred in the areas under the jurisdiction of the Lao Zha and Central Police Stations. Considering the large number of watch stores within the concession, these cases are relatively few. Considering the valuable and easily targeted nature of the goods in watch stores, the thoroughness of police protection is evident. In the above-mentioned two cases, one was on Fuzhou Road and the other was on Nanjing Road. The police sentries were only sixty yards and less than twenty-five yards away from the scene of the incident, respectively. The victims did not report the robbery at the time but only called for help after the robbers had fled. Within the above-mentioned time, the Lao Zha Police District alone had fifty-three robbery cases, and eighty-three people were arrested by the police, seventy-one of whom have been sentenced. The effectiveness of the police in dealing with robbers is evident. This letter is for your information." The association has forwarded the letter to the Watch Industry Association for their information.

Chen Xianglin's Nationality Issue 172

Arrested by the Public Security Bureau for Promoting Communism and About to be Handed Over, He Suddenly Claimed to be of Japanese Nationality, Unexpectedly, the Japanese Consulate Was About to Arrest Him, and Chen Then Claimed to Have Escaped from a Revolution in Taiwan to Shanghai

As a Result, Chen Was Temporarily Handed Over to the Municipal Council for Detention 173

Chen Xianglin, a Taiwanese, also known as Weng Zesheng, Weng Guosheng, and Li Guoliang, was sentenced to one year in prison by the court in 1919 for promoting communism in Shanghai. Later, on appeal, the sentence was reduced to three months. After serving his sentence, Chen had also been wanted in Taiwan and Hong Kong for promoting communism after he escaped from the island. The Japanese Consulate and the British and French Concession Police Stations in this city all had his photograph and notification. On the afternoon of the 4th of this month, detectives from the Public Security Bureau, acting on orders to arrest him for promoting communism, apprehended him on the way to Wenjian Master Road and escorted him to the police station. On Sunday morning, he was escorted to the High Court Second Branch for questioning. Lawyer Zhan Jifeng represented the Public Security Bureau, requesting that he be handed over for questioning. According to Chen's confession, he was originally from Fujian and denied the alleged promotion. Judge Yu Yeting ruled in court that the defendant be handed over for further investigation. Unexpectedly, after the court's ruling, the defendant suddenly claimed that he was originally from Taiwan and should not be subject to the Chinese court, declaring his opposition. He also claimed that the Japanese Consulate could prove that he was Taiwanese. The police then dispatched Deputy Detective Mao Yiwen to the Japanese Consulate for investigation. It was then learned that the Japanese Consulate was also wanted to arrest him, and the police station also had a record of his case. At 3 PM in the afternoon, Judge Yu held another court session at the Criminal Division One of the High Court. Secretariat Officer Masayuki Hashizume and Mr. Minsan Maeda, who had previously worked at the Taiwan Governor's Office for twenty years, appeared in court on behalf of the Japanese Consulate. According to Masayuki Hashizume, the defendant's original name was Li Guoliang, who was born in Taiwan and was wanted by the authorities for promoting communism. Therefore, he fled to Hong Kong, where he was deported for ten years and then came to Shanghai. Because he came to Shanghai secretly, he has no passport or other documents to verify, but Minsan Maeda, who has worked at the Taiwan Governor's Office for many years, can recognize him. Then, Minsan Maeda said that the defendant was born in the Taipingcho area of Taipei without error. Lawyer Gan Jingxian representing the police stated that now that the defendant has been proven to be of Japanese nationality, he should be handed over to the Japanese Consulate. Lawyer Zhan Jifeng, representing the Public Security Bureau, stated that the defendant had previously been punished by the Chinese court and had not claimed to be of Japanese nationality. Even at the beginning of today's trial, he did not mention his Japanese nationality until the court approved the transfer. Since the Japanese Consulate can prove that he is Taiwanese, the defendant may have dual nationality. Therefore, he requested the court to handle the case according to the law, or temporarily detain him to investigate his nationality before further action. At that time, the defendant suddenly claimed that he had revolted in Taiwan and escaped to Shanghai. Therefore, he opposed the transfer by the Public Security Bureau and the Japanese Consulate and demanded immediate release. The court ordered that he be temporarily handed over to the Municipal Council for detention.

Coroner's Examination of the Tragic Death of a Worker Due to a Fall 174

Zhou Changsheng, a 44-year-old local from No. 236 Pinlang Road, worked as a laborer in the weaving section of the Tongxing Yarn Factory at No. 1443 Gordon Road. At around 2:00 PM the day before yesterday, the machine belt suddenly came off the shaft. Zhou then climbed to a height of fifteen feet above the ground to reattach the belt, but lost his balance and his left hand was caught in the belt. He fell to the ground in extreme pain, injuring his head, hands, and other parts. He immediately fainted. Another worker, Li Xiaodi, saw this and immediately reported it to the factory staff, who in turn reported it to the Putuo Road Police Station, ordering detectives to send the injured man to Baolong Hospital for treatment. He died soon after despite the treatment. The body was taken to the Fei Lun Road Coroner's Office. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Court was requested to send Prosecutor Guo Wei to the office to examine the body, take the stand, and record the case. According to the testimony of Li Xiaodi, Zhou was reattaching the belt that day but accidentally attached it to another shaft, causing his left hand to be crushed and him to fall. According to the statement of Zhou Zhou's wife, she requested compensation from the factory. According to the statement of the factory representative, Japanese national Iwabayashi Takeo, the deceased was indeed a worker in the factory. Now that he died on duty, they would give compensation. After receiving the statement, Guo ruled that Zhou Changsheng died from injuries sustained during the fall, and the body was released to his wife Zhou Zhou, who made a written guarantee to take it back for burial.

Tragic Bathing Accident 176

丨Liu Huisheng Accidentally Enters Boiling Water and Scalds to Death丨

Liu Huisheng, a 50-year-old from Jiangbei, was a stone barge boatman. On the 24th of last month, his boat passed through Minhang and he stopped there. He went ashore to take a bath at the First Bathhouse. Unexpectedly, he accidentally entered the boiling water pool. By the time he felt the pain and stood up, the lower half of his body was already red and swollen and the skin had peeled off. He immediately left the bathhouse and collapsed outside, unable to move. He was rushed to the hospital for treatment, but he had been poisoned by the heat and there was no good medicine. He finally died yesterday. Because he had no family members, the township chief reported to the local court for a coroner's examination. Prosecutor Yang An and others were appointed to examine the scene and determined that he had died from scalding. They ruled that if no family members arrived, the bathhouse would arrange for the burial.

Reader Consultant 182

Reading and Love 183

丨丨From Gu Yingjun丨丨

My life, the happiness of my future, everything about me, is now flying in a storm-like environment. Sometimes I feel sad, but sometimes ideals make me feel excited. My own outlook on life has always been aimless, because of my environment. Therefore, I often think to myself, "Where is the destination of my life?" Ah! I am gradually getting older, I am already a "person" of seventeen years old. I am confident that my will is enough to deal with my environment, but my own knowledge is limited because of the economic constraints of my family in my childhood. It is really pitiful to say that I have not yet reached the level of a primary school graduate. However, because I have been reading newspapers in public reading places every day during the years I have been out of school, this is my only hobby, so I have also gained some practical knowledge. But now, I feel the depression of "the destination of life." Therefore, I live in ideals every day. But I have realized, Mr. Reporter, I will tell you what I will ask for. I am confident that my personality is suitable for studying philosophy, but I am also interested in social sciences and natural sciences, especially in literary research and aesthetic appreciation. Mr. Reporter, my will and my future destination are all clearly dissected in the above-mentioned few points. Therefore, I am now asking a question for you to answer: It is of course possible for me to enter school, so of course, there is only one way for me to study philosophy, social sciences, natural sciences, and literary aesthetics, and that is self-study. But my will is very vague. How should the path of self-study be taken? Mr. Reporter, don't think it's ridiculous. Although I don't have great talent, I firmly believe that my ambition tells me, "I will become a second Goethe (J.W. Goethe)!" Mr. Reporter, do you find it ridiculous? How will I finish reading the books of the above-mentioned subjects? Although books can never be finished, this is another opinion of mine. Please answer me, sir. After that, I would like to ask you to solve a common disease of young people: love. Although love is the most needed thing for young people, I am still very suspicious of love in my current environment. Does love hinder reading? How can I avoid it and not talk about love? How can one be worthy of talking about love? Not the love of mammonism, but the love of Mirl. Due to the urgency of time, everything I wrote is very clumsy and contradictory, so I hope you will understand this.

Answer: After reading your letter, my reply is as follows: (1) Studying does not necessarily require going to school (this is naturally a last resort). You can read books in public reading places and in circulating libraries. Moreover, studying in this way is carried out in the struggle of life. This kind of studying is living study, not dead study. If you want to study philosophy, you can first read the following books: "Fundamental Problems of Social Science" translated by Li Da (Xinxian Bookstore), "Historical Materialism" (Modern Bookstore), "Classics of Dialectics" (Yadong). After reading the above three books, you will naturally find the path to the various sciences you want to study. (2) You "want to be a second Goethe," I advise you not to. Naturally, the 18th-century Goethe is worthy of our admiration. However, at most, our admiration of Goethe as a natural scientist and writer is the same as our admiration of Kant as a natural scientist and philosopher. Neither of them are spokespersons for the working masses. Goethe later became an aristocrat. We modern people do not need a second Goethe, because he cannot represent our call to resist imperialism, and he cannot inspire us to fight against evil forces. We do not need a second Goethe. We at least need a second Gorky, a second Barbusse, a second Sinclair. May you strive for this! (3) Love is not absolutely harmful. However, it is absolutely harmful to a young person who is frivolous in nature, unstable in blood and qi, has little experience, and is under the age of twenty. At least it is 99% harmful, the so-called "more harm than good"! There is no good way to avoid it. You can only make up your mind to study knowledge. If you put in real effort into literature, art, or philosophy and other historical sciences, you will naturally find it very interesting. At that time, your spirit may be attached to something, and you will not talk about love all day long. Finally, I would like to ask, the reporter rarely pays attention to love. What book did you see about the "Mirl-style love" you mentioned? Please teach me.

Page 12

Free Talk

From Satire to Humor 184

— He Jiagan

A satirist is dangerous.

If what he satirizes are the illiterate, the slaughtered, the imprisoned, and the oppressed, then that's great. It just gives the so-called educated intellectuals who read his articles a chuckle. It makes them feel even braver and more intelligent. However, the reason why satirists today are satirists is precisely because they satirize this group of so-called educated intellectuals.

Because what is satirized is this group of society, each member feels as if they have been stabbed themselves, so they each come out secretly and use their satire to try to stab the satirist to death.

First, they say he is cynical, and gradually they say he is scolding, wisecracking, venomous, hateful, an academic bandit, a Shaoxing lawyer, and so on. However, the satire of society often remains "amazingly long." Even if they bring out a foreign monk or start a tabloid to attack, it is still ineffective. How can this not infuriate people!

The crux is here: what he satirizes is society. If society does not change, this satire will continue to exist. What you stab is him personally. If his satire exists, your satire will fall flat.

Therefore, to overthrow such a hateful satirist, one can only change this society.

However, social satirists are dangerous, especially in an era when some "writers" openly and secretly become "the king's claws." Who is happy to be the protagonist in a "literary inquisition"? But if they don't die completely, there will always be a breath of resentment in their stomach, which they want to spit out with a chuckle, using laughter as a guise. Laughter does not offend others, and there is no provision in the current law that citizens must wear a mourning face. It is not "illegal," so it can be asserted.

I think this is the reason why "humor" has become popular in writing since last year. However, there are naturally many who are simply "laughing for the sake of laughing."

However, this situation will probably not last long. "Humor" is not a domestic product, and the Chinese are not a people who are good at "humor." Moreover, it is really difficult to be humorous now. Therefore, even humor is bound to change its appearance. It either leans towards social satire or falls into traditional "jokes" and "seeking cheap advantages."

"Hu Shih and Guo Moruo" 185

— Zhou Leshan

The book "Hu Shih and Guo Moruo," which was heavily advertised in 1932 and published in February 1933, is three inches thick, truly a "massive" work unprecedented. I plan to spend a month of evenings reading it. Tonight, I begin to open the cover. The first page features a portrait of the copyright holder, Mr. Tan, to verify the book's copyright. On the second page, I discovered an extraordinary piece of writing, which I dare not keep to myself and respectfully transcribe below for the shared enjoyment of all.

Sent to Hu Shih and Guo Moruo

Don't say that a little fellow is nothing / Speaking carelessly and irresponsibly

Can't you see the blind man with the "hoe"!

Miscellaneous Current Affairs Thoughts 186

— Bo Fu

One

Matsuoka Yosuke told reporters that China's boycott of Japanese goods and purchase of military supplies is tantamount to suicide (see yesterday's newspaper). I suppose Japan is killing China because it doesn't want to see China commit suicide?

Two

Yesterday's newspaper reported that a blind fortune teller fell in love with a blind woman who already had a husband while telling her fortune, and they had a physical relationship. Is love truly blind?

Three

A certain boring publication carried a letter from a reader to Mr. Li Lieh-wen, editor of "Free Talk," calling Mr. Zeng's "lyrics" (?) an immortal work. In fact, Mr. Zeng has already clearly told us "Now it's possible," so why should the reader flatter him excessively?

Four

During the initial period of the Fourth State, one could still hear people singing "Little Sister, I Love You," but it hasn't been heard for a long time now. Perhaps men have all realized that "Little Sister, You Love Me" is the right way, right?

My Lover 187

— Ai Wu

Two idle and bored friends, how annoying, actually started making fun of me. They linked a completely unrelated little woman to me, stubbornly assigning her as my lover; both of them speaking at once, not allowing me to explain at all. As a result, I got angry and retorted with even some unpleasant words. But calmly thinking about it, their unreasonable teasing didn't come out of thin air. Because whenever I heard that little woman singing mournful songs, I would unconsciously reveal a sad mood on my face and in my words.

This laughable and annoying incident happened in the Lockup on the shore of the Indian Ocean in Rangoon; my two friends and I were imprisoned by British imperialism for violating Article X of the Indian government's law, supposedly for committing crimes endangering the local government. It was in early 1931. The room inside the Lockup was quite nice, with electric lights and a Western-style toilet, nothing was lacking. Compared to the Burmese house I lived in in the Alon area outside Rangoon, in any case, my material life could be considered to have greatly stepped up a level. But living there for a long time became annoying, especially since it lacked the essential element of life: freedom. Perhaps because the three Chinese were all political prisoners, we were separated from the other prisoners as soon as we entered; thus, one room became the world occupied by the three of us. And the three of us were quite familiar with each other on the outside, so in this boring world, we simply couldn't find any fresh or interesting stories to talk about. Everyone only created interest by fabricating stories about each other that were neither funny nor annoying. That's how we spent the entire day playing games of teasing each other. There was also one other happy thing, which was that after lunch every day, the Indian guard with the mustache would open the iron gate and let us take a walk on an open-air corridor behind the building, look up at the kind blue sky, and always happily raise our arms, wanting to completely swallow the fresh air into our lungs. Sometimes, seeing an unknown bird flashing its black wings across the clear sky, our fleeting thoughts seemed to be carried away by its wings, and a faint homesickness followed in our lonely hearts. Across the corridor, a row of smaller rooms stood, with sparsely drooping green vines hanging from the eaves, and a black lacquered wooden sign hanging on the door that read "Female Cage." This aroused our curiosity, and every time we took a walk, we would quietly stand under the window for a while, planning to see the female prisoners inside. But every time it was gloomy, filled only with loneliness, without a single figure.

One night, suddenly a woman's singing came from the Female Cage side, and we, who were sitting listlessly, were all captivated by the singing, holding our breath and listening.

"·················"

Ah, I recognize who you are!

Wasn't it you venomous snakes

Who killed my husband in the mango grove?

You burned down my thatched hut,

And now you've arrested me,

Please, if you want to beat me, beat me, if you want to kill me, kill me,

You venomous snakes!

·············"

An Indian man with a mustache shouted loudly to stop her, and the singing stopped immediately, like a broken string on a Chinese violin.

"What a pitiful woman!" This sigh sprang suddenly from my heart as if ejected by a spring. Although my two friends didn't quite understand this Burmese song, the sadness and misery of the female voice also penetrated their hearts; therefore, a pulse of pity and sympathy immediately floated between their eyebrows. Late at night, when the Indian guard with a large bunch of keys on his waist walked to the iron gate to check, we found some things to ask about the female prisoner who sang. From his reluctant mouth, we couldn't find out much, but we roughly knew that the woman with the mournful singing was indeed a "robber woman" captured from the Tharrawaddy District. Who doesn't know that the Tharrawaddy District was the origin of the Burmese peasant riots in December 1930? That woman was undoubtedly the wife of an anti-imperialist warrior. Thus, in my heart, which had pity for her, a solemn respect was unconsciously added. And from the meaning of the woman's song, I understood why the rioting peasants used such a strange flag. Before I was arrested, I had seen a flag seized from the peasants by the British government, a triangular piece of white cloth, depicting a large snake covered in scales, struggling on the ground under the feet of a majestic god. The god had a thunder god's mouth, a small pagoda on his head, and a pair of wings growing on his elbows; his left hand tightly grasped the snake's tail, and the knife in his right hand was in a position to chop it down - this was clearly a silhouette of the British-Burmese struggle, and the giant snake was not exactly a symbol of imperialism poisoning all of Burma?

In 1931 Burma, which was just beginning to roar, a mixed team of footsteps, accompanied by the noise of iron chains, scraped harshly into the gloomy corridor in front of the iron gate every day. Embedding our eyes in the cracks in the iron bars, we saw the shadows of peasants with shaved heads and tattoos, wearing red and green cloth skirts, with worried, brown-yellow, thin faces, passing by one by one. Occasionally, there were also monks wearing yellow kasayas and bare half-arms, drooping their shiny heads, being escorted along with them. But these prisoners, passing through in no more than a day or two, were all reassigned to the Rangoon Central Prison. Remaining in this Lockup were only some prisoners with less serious cases. As for the singing "robber woman," she was detained here for a relatively long time, perhaps just because she was a woman? (To be continued)

The Story of the Black Woman Seeking God (20) 189

— By Xiao Boren, translated by Yi Xian

"What is a 'tie kai'?" the Arab said, smoothing out his long robe to make the pleats lie flat.

"It's a three-cent coin," said the magician. "Why was this made? Because wealthy people are embarrassed to be seen giving me copper coins, and they think that six cents is too much."

"I don't like being treated like that," the Arab said. "Much also has a mission to convey. If my people are left to their own devices, they will prostrate themselves before all the images on the head. If there are no images, they will worship stones. My mission is to convey that only the unique, glorious, and great God has majesty and power. No one has ever dared to make an image of him; if anyone tries to commit such a crime, I will forget God's mercy, overcome my weakness, and simply kill that person with my own hands. Who can imagine the greatness of God in a physical form? Even an excellent image of a horse cannot convey a bit of his beauty, his greatness. Well, when I tell them this, they also ask me to perform magic tricks, and I tell them that I am the same as them, that God himself cannot violate his own laws. If he can imagine doing something unlawful, then they go away and proclaim that I am performing miracles. They also believe, because if they doubt, I have the believers kill them. You should do the same, friend."

"The mission that I convey is that they should not kill each other," said the magician. "People must have a spirit of unity."

"As far as their private disputes are concerned," this is true, the Arab said. "But we must kill those who are not fit to live. It is important to water the garden, but it is also important to pull weeds."

"Who will be the judge of our fitness to live?" said the magician. "The highest government officials, the governors of the empire, and the high priests all think that I am not fit to live. Perhaps they are right."

"As for myself, they made the same decision," said the Arab. "I had to flee. I kept hiding until I told the healthy young men - enough people - that their elders had misunderstood me: in fact, the truth was not like that. So I came back with those healthy young men and pulled weeds in the garden."

"I admire your courage and practical cleverness," said the magician. "But I was not born that way."

"You don't need to admire such qualities," said the Arab. "I feel a little ashamed of this. Aren't all desert elders expressing these qualities well? What I value about myself is the transcendence of my soul, which makes me a medium for divine inspiration. Have you ever written a book?"

"No," the magician said sadly. "I wish I had that ability, then I would earn a lot of money and be able to escape this hateful cross and publish my mission to spread it throughout the world. But I am not a writer. I have compiled a simple prayer, in which, I think, there may be various essences. But God has given me the inspiration to speak, not the inspiration to write."

"Writing is useful," said the Arab. "I was inspired and wrote many chapters of the word of God, may his name be praised! But there are also people in this world who want God to take care of them, but it is impossible. His word means nothing to them; so whenever I have to deal with them, I am no longer inspired and have to rely on my own inventions and my own wit. I write all sorts of terrible stories for them, some about the Last Judgment, some about the hell where evildoers will suffer forever. I contrast these horrors with the paradise prepared for those who do God's will. It is this kind of paradise that will tempt them, you understand! It is a paradise with gardens, fragrances, and beautiful women."

Yu Qing-tang to Denmark 190

To Investigate Mass Education

(Nanjing, 6th) The Ministry of Education has dispatched Yu Qing-tang to Denmark to investigate mass education, and has requested the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to notify the Danish Embassy.

(Jinan, 6th) This morning, Han Fu-qu went to the Provincial First Normal School and summoned more than a thousand students to speak, roughly saying that normal school students must abstain from indulgence and extravagance, and in the future, when they become teachers, they will change China's customs.

Standing Committee of the Chinese Education Association 192

The Chinese Education Association was established in Shanghai in January of this year. At that time, it was resolved that the General Association should be located at the Education College of National Central University in Nanjing. Yesterday (the 4th), the first meeting of the Standing Committee was held in the Education College of Central University. Those present included Chang Dao-zhi, Chen Li-jiang, Zheng Xi-gu, Xu Ke-tu, and others. The following important cases were resolved: (1) How to urge fundraising for association expenses: it was resolved that (1) donation booklets should be printed and distributed to local leaders to raise funds before April 15th, and remit them to the association, (2) request educational administrative agencies to subsidize the association's expenses. (2) The association's case for registration: it was resolved that a work plan for the association should be drafted and submitted to the Central Party Headquarters for registration and to the Ministry of Education for filing. (3) How to stipulate the association's work plan: it was resolved that (1) a plan should be formulated and earnestly implemented based on the matters listed in the third clause of the association's general charter and the fourth, sixth, and seventh clauses of the first board meeting, (2) the association should conduct surveys of the economic conditions of urban and rural populations and the education they need, and the steps for this are as follows: A. Members Shao Shuang-qiu and Gu Mei should each draft specific survey methods and submit them to the association before April; B. The branches should contact relevant local organizations and conduct the survey together; (3) the association should entrust educational institutions to carry out the following experimental work: A. Entrust Jiangsu Educational College to carry out an experiment on popularizing mass education; B. Entrust Beijing Normal University Affiliated Elementary School, Guangzhou Central University Affiliated Elementary School, Hubei Provincial First Elementary School, Jiangxi Nanchang Municipal First Elementary School, Kaifeng Henan University Affiliated Elementary School, etc., to conduct experimental education on production; C. Entrust Jiangsu Huangdu Township Teachers School to conduct work-study experiments; (4) it was resolved that the association should send a letter to National Central University to borrow rooms as the association's headquarters; (5) it was resolved that the association should send a letter to urge all localities to establish branches as soon as possible and report the date of establishment; (6) it was resolved that the association should publish [Association Members' Newsletter]; (7) it was resolved that the association should send a letter to Mr. Zheng Xiaoqia to proceed with publishing matters; (8) it was resolved that the association should send a letter to Mr. Zhuang Zexuan to proceed with the matter of reviewing educational names; (9) the case of Mao Bao-yu, the association's fundraising committee member in Anqing, Anhui, requesting resignation due to personal reasons: it was resolved to change the appointment to member Hao Zhao-chu; (10) it was resolved that the next meeting of the Standing Committee of the association should be held at Wuxi Educational College, with the date set for the afternoon of May 13th.

Opening of Provincial Zhenjiang Library 193

The Provincial Zhenjiang Library in Taiping Bridge, Zhenjiang City, was opened on the 5th. The library has a newspaper reading room, a magazine reading room, and two book reading rooms. The newspaper room has dozens of newspapers from the provincial capital, Beijing-Shanghai, Ping-Han, and English and Japanese newspapers. The magazine room has four or five hundred kinds of Chinese and foreign periodicals of various subjects, all displayed on shelves for people to read. The reference shelves in the book reading room also have dozens of kinds of dictionaries and reference books of various subjects. The card catalogs are full of monthly record cards, arranged by category, making it extremely convenient to check. Those who borrow books fill out forms, and the borrowing procedures are very fast. There is also a survey form for statistics. There are instructors in the room to guide the inspection methods and the use of reference books at any time, which is very thoughtful. The library currently has 30,000 to 40,000 books, and many more are ordered from Pingguang and foreign countries but have not yet arrived. However, the library's location is currently rented, and the location is also relatively remote. It is heard that they are currently planning to build their own building. If a new-style library building can be built in a suitable location, it can become the cultural center of the provincial capital. Yesterday was the first month of opening. According to afternoon statistics, there were more than 300 readers in the newspaper and magazine reading rooms, and about 100 to 200 readers in the book reading room. The books read were mostly in literature and social sciences. The library is open as usual on Sunday mornings and afternoons, and is closed on Monday for holidays. In order to facilitate civil servants, it is also open for two hours every evening from Tuesday to Saturday.

Resignation News of Kunshan Education Bureau Director 194

Since the principal of Kunshan County Middle School was ordered by the province to have the director of the county's Education Bureau reappoint qualified personnel and submit them to the Education Department for approval, the director has reported twice, but both times the qualifications were not met and were criticized. Recently, it was read that the Education Department criticized the director for improper handling, and the director has resigned to the Education Department.

Anti-Japanese Zeal in Tsinghua and Yenching Universities in Beiping 197

Tsinghua Female Students Sew First Aid Kits; Yenching University Purchases Ten Thousand Steel Helmets

Elementary and Secondary School Students Donate Two Thousand Dollars; Peking University and Normal University are Quiet

(Special dispatch from Beiping) Among the four national universities, seven ministry-run universities, twelve private universities, five private college-level vocational schools, nine municipal middle schools, fifty private middle schools, fifty-eight municipal elementary schools, one hundred and fourteen private elementary schools, twenty-two social education institutions, twenty-four municipal people's schools, and thirty-five private people's schools, a total of 248 schools and institutions with more than 130,000 students, Peking University has always been known as a leading school. During the past May Fourth Movement and the March 18 Massacre, its students suffered the most sacrifices. Since the September 18th Incident, National Tsinghua University, Normal University, the Law School of Peiping University, and private Pingmin University and Yenching University have emerged as rising stars, successively engaging in anti-Japanese movements and being more enthusiastic than Peking University. However, Peking University students are also unwilling to lag behind, so their demonstration southward is different in meaning from the petitions of other universities. However, recently, with the crisis in Rehe, Peiping and Tianjin are in danger, not only Peking University students have not expressed anything, even the Law School, Normal University, and Pingmin University, which were rising stars, have not had any spectacular patriotic movements, only Tsinghua University and Yenching University in the city of Peiping are doing practical anti-Japanese work. The students of municipal and private elementary and secondary schools are younger and are mostly guided by teachers. This time, the fundraising for anti-Japanese donations is also temporarily assisted by the principals and teachers of various schools. Outsiders suspect that with the tension in Rehe, the students of various universities in Beiping are quiet, and the reporter has specially investigated the reasons for the students' silence in various universities and the anti-Japanese work of Tsinghua and Yenching Universities and the donation situation of elementary and secondary school students, as follows:

Peking University and Normal University are Silent 198

Students at various universities in Peiping,

except for Tsinghua and Yenching

Universities, mostly remain silent. The

reasons are five: (1) Peking University has

been embroiled in a school principal expulsion

storm since last year due to the issue of delaying

tuition fees. As a result, several student

representatives were expelled. Three months ago,

forty-odd male and female students were arrested for holding an anti-Japanese

meeting. Later, the anti-Japanese association of

the school virtually came to a standstill due to

differing opinions among students

regarding the direction of anti-Japanese activities. (2) The reason for

Normal University is that there has been no principal for ten

days. There was once a large principal riot. After

the September 18th Incident, students also

petitioned southward one after another. All student

leaders and central figures in the principal riots

were expelled from school by the principal three

months ago under the order of the Ministry of

Education. Since then, the student union

committee has been scattered and no one is

advising the patriotic movement. (3)

The famous professors welcomed by students at

the University of Technology, Ma Zemin, Hou Wailu, and De Heng,

were arrested on suspicion of being Communists, and

as many as forty-five students were arrested in succession.

The remaining students also stood by indifferently, and even dared

not become leaders of anti-Japanese associations.

Tsinghua Female Students Sew Kits 199

The Tsinghua University Student Union's Anti-

Japanese National Salvation Association received five

thousand emergency first aid kits. The

entire school of female students and professors' wives

began sewing them. They work daily

in the Gongzi Hall.

Each female student and professor's wife sew non-stop,

sewing densely. Among them, someone said,

With the Rehe situation being critical, frontline soldiers

are sacrificing themselves for the country. Women should

do their best to contribute at this time of crisis,

to express their condolences. Also, students from

the school's engineering school, ten

students, organized

a wireless radio association, which facilitates practice,

and once they will apply scientific capabilities to

national defense preparations, for scientific

national salvation. The association has already been established,

electing Jiang Baozeng as president,

Sun Ruiliu as the reporting director,

Zhu Songwei as the machine affairs director,

Bao Xinian as the accounting director,

and Ding Zhengyi as the secretary director.

Yenching University Orders Steel Helmets 200

The steel helmet movement at Yenching University

has become a reality since the student

side ordered one thousand helmets,

and the faculty and staff side has ordered

three thousand nine hundred helmets,

bringing the total, with the student side, to

four thousand nine hundred helmets. The remaining

purchasing method is either by donation,

or by order. As for the first batch

of one thousand steel helmets ordered,

they will be completed and in stock within a week.

It is heard that the goal of the school

is to raise enough to purchase ten thousand steel

helmets. The anti-Japanese association has

decided on six principles for distributing steel

helmets: (1) Troops currently fighting against

Japan; (2) Armies previously organized with discipline;

(3) Armies capable of fighting;

(4) Armies currently in critical war zones;

(5) Personally delivered to the front by the student

anti-Japanese association; (6) Carefully and evenly distributed.

Launching the Big Pancake Movement 201

Liu Facheng, a worker at Yenching University, deeply concerned about the lack of food supplies at the front lines and the difficulties in transportation, and moved by the sight of soldiers fighting on empty stomachs, has voluntarily initiated a "Big Pancake Movement." These pancakes are "as big as a wok, about one foot in diameter and three inches thick, each weighing about ten catties and costing about seventy cents." He appeals to the public to emulate this donation and send them to the front lines for the soldiers to eat. Mr. Liu has a large pancake, the Yenching University Student Anti-Japanese Association has one, and he requests that donations be quickly initiated. The association will hang the pancake high, display it downstairs in the building, and set up a donation box, asking students to donate freely. It is planned to move it to other places for display in the coming days to solicit donations from all sides. From 4:00 PM to 5:00 PM every day, responsible staff members Tan Haiying and Zhang Desheng will be in charge of receiving donations at the Anti-Japanese Association office, so that this glorious and majestic classroom will have one more large pancake on display.

Primary and Secondary School Students Raise Funds 202

Students from public and private primary and secondary schools in Beiping have eagerly and voluntarily raised funds since receiving donor registration books from the Education Association, achieving remarkable results. The amount of donations is highest from Pei-Man Girls' High School, as it is a school with many aristocratic young ladies. The donations from faculty and staff of municipal primary and secondary schools are deducted from their salaries by the Social Affairs Bureau and submitted to the Donations United Association for delivery to the Education Association. The student donations alone total 2,188 yuan, 7 jiao, and 2 fen.

Municipal Education Bureau Orders Primary and Secondary Schools to Add Sanitary and Sports Facilities 203

The Municipal Education Bureau yesterday issued an order to all primary and secondary schools in the city, stating that sanitation and physical education are essential for the strength of young children’s bodies and the health of their minds. Schools should pay close attention to them and implement them diligently, as previously ordered. However, having adequate sanitation and sports facilities will greatly facilitate implementation. Schools should add as many of these as possible within the possible range of operating expenses to facilitate teaching and learning. This order is hereby issued for compliance.

Military Song (Three) by Luo Jialun 204

(Dedicated to the Anti-Japanese People of the Northeast)

China's three northeastern provinces,

Have the most fertile land.

Black earth is black,

Sorghum is tall,

The north wind rises and the horse herds are proud.

Changbai Mountain is covered in white snow,

The Yalu River surges and roars.

Our ancestors toiled diligently to develop this land.

Who dares to invade and occupy it?

Let him first try my blade.

If a man is born without courage to kill the enemy,

Even in death, he cannot be considered a hero!

At this time when the national war for survival has begun, there should be inspiring and passionate military songs to strengthen the morale of the army and encourage the spirit of the people. However, what has been heard in recent years has mostly been decadent music, which causes me deep concern. Therefore, I have written several military songs. Mr. Tang Xueyong, a music expert, saw them and praised them, promising to compose music for them. Thus, I, despite my humble talents, present them to the world. The inadequacy of the lyrics is truly due to the surging national consciousness that I cannot restrain myself. The music for the first song has already been composed and will be printed after correction. The music for the second and third songs is being prepared and will also be printed soon. Because many people have written to Mr. Tang requesting the sheet music, it is planned to print these three songs together with the lyrics into a small booklet for distribution. Those who need it can write directly to the Publishing Group of Nanjing Central University to request it. Domestic writers should feel the same at this time of deep crisis and urgent disaster. If we can use this opportunity to cultivate a magnificent and powerful literary sound to express the great spirit of the Chinese nation, this is truly what I sincerely pray for. My humble work is insignificant. Luo Jialun respectfully notes.

Xinmin Middle School Gradually Returns to Its Former Glory 209

Jiangwan Xinmin Middle School used to be very developed and was one of the best-run private schools in Shanghai. During the January 28th Incident last year, the school moved to the concession to hold classes. All the equipment and books in the Jiangwan school were looted, and part of the school building was destroyed, resulting in a huge loss. Last autumn, the school moved back to the Jiangwan site to hold classes, but many students hesitated to come because they listened to rumors, so the number of students was not large. Now, after more than half a year of rectification, the school has gradually returned to its former glory, and the number of students has increased to more than 200. In order to actively expand, the school has scheduled a board meeting around the 20th of this month to discuss everything. It is said that Qu Jinqing, Chuan Ruoyu, Liu Zhanen, Zheng Zhangcheng and other school directors have agreed to participate.

Shanghai Art College Student National Crisis Propaganda Troupe 210

Students of the Shanghai Art College organized a National Crisis Propaganda Team, created a large number of shocking national crisis paintings, and exhibited them publicly to give the public a direct impression. Last month, the team went to Nanjing to hold a National Crisis Painting Exhibition, which greatly shocked the people of the capital. Later, with the support of Chairman Lin and the Central Party Headquarters, they planned to go to Anhui, Henan, Hubei, Hunan, Jiangxi and Jiangsu for long-distance propaganda to awaken the people in the interior. It is reported that the Art College received a report yesterday from the team in Hubei that all propaganda work has been approved by the Wuhan Provincial Party Headquarters, and more than a dozen team members, including Shen Yiqian, are staying at the Provincial Party Headquarters. American Basketball Expert Talks About the Situation of Basketball Spreading to Countries Around the World 227

Twenty Million People Around the World Play Basketball for Men and Women

America Will Send a Team to Perform at the Next Olympic Games

(Lawrence, USA, 6th) American basketball expert Forrest C. Allen, Chairman of the American National Basketball Coaches Association and member of the Olympic Committee, talked about the benefits of basketball competition and the situation around the world. According to statistics, the number of men and women in the public who play basketball today has reached 20 million, and almost every country is actively promoting this competition.

Countries Where Basketball Has Spread 228

The countries where basketball competition has become popular are France, Italy, China, Japan, Persia, India, Sweden, the Philippines, Portugal, Czechoslovakia, Turkey, Greece, Mexico, Canada, Poland, Russia, Germany, Britain, and various countries in South America, all of which have basketball competition.

The Process of Spreading to Europe 229

The International YMCA has of course spread this competition from the Americas to various countries for a long time, and after the European War, the American Army's teaching of basketball in Europe was a major reason for popularizing it in Europe. In 1900, the American Army taught basketball to the Philippines. In 1918, after the European War, the American Army that occupied Germany taught basketball to the Germans. In 1919, the American, French, and Italian Allies held a triangular championship in Paris. The United States won easily. After the signing of the peace treaty, the two American teams, at the invitation of the British government, performed in the British zone of the war zone. The British were happy to learn it.

The Olympic Games Did Not Adopt It 230

Almost all countries in the world use the American basketball rules as the standard, because the United States is the mother country of basketball, so they all follow it. At the Olympic Games held in Los Angeles last autumn, Allen proposed to the committee to use basketball competition as a performance. All countries expressed their support and interest, but the Americans did not pay attention to it and support it. As a result, the committee, due to economic income, changed to using American football as a performance. People in various countries knew less about it and paid less attention to it.

International Interest Is Growing 231

With the widespread adoption of basketball competition, it is likely to be adopted at the Olympic Games to be held in Berlin in 1936. The recent visit of the Mexican team and the Meiji University basketball team of Japan to the United States proves that international interest is growing. Both teams were warmly welcomed and successful in the United States. According to a letter to Allen from the coach of Waseda University in Japan, if there had been basketball at the Olympic Games last autumn, Japan would have sent participants. A common opinion is that at the next Olympic Games, the United States should select two teams to perform once, because the subtle techniques of the United States in this field are truly beyond the reach of other countries.

Unprecedented Plunge in the Gold Market

The United States Will Abandon the Gold Standard, Prohibiting Cash Exports

The Market Suddenly Lost Its Normal State, and People Fell into Absolute Terror

The Opening Plunge Was Forty-Nine Taels and Seven Mace, at 698 Taels

The Lowest Point Reached 660 Taels, Showing Long-Distance Fluctuations

Falling Madly by Sixty-Six Taels and Seven Mace at a Difference of Forty-Three Taels

Recently, the gold market has been favorable to short sellers, but it seemed that there was a need to hover for a while. Who would have known that after Roosevelt took office as president, the financial turmoil suddenly expanded? The call to abolish the gold standard became even louder, and countries stopped all dealings with US exchange rates, fearing unexpected drastic changes. People were in a state of absolute panic. The Gold Exchange originally planned to open after the HSBC US exchange rate was posted, so it was delayed until after 9:30. When HSBC's posting was revealed, the telegraphic transfer rate remained unchanged, but the US exchange rate had no price. The Gold Exchange suddenly opened, and the calling prices were chaotic, at 698 taels, already breaking through the 700 taels mark, plunging more than 40 taels. However, people's panic had reached its peak, and sellers were still numerous. The decline was rapid, and in an instant, it plunged 38 taels, sharply dropping to 660 taels. Afterwards, because there were still many short covering, it rose by ten, but there were occasional long-distance fluctuations. The US exchange rate saw transactions at this point, and it was bound to be much looser than the previous close, and there was no time to consider it. Telegraphic transfer rates in the market were also good, and there were quite a few people covering shorts at low prices in the market. However, large long positions such as Hengxing and Fuchang remained silent because they did not acknowledge the opening price. Buyers were hit hard, and the gold price once rebounded more than 40 taels, reaching 703 taels. However, the market price changed extremely quickly, with large ups and downs. The afternoon opening saw a horizontal plunge, to 676 taels, and then to 84 taels. The exchange rate was still strong, falling to 64 taels, and then leveling off. In reality, short sellers took advantage of the low price to maintain their positions, so it was pulled up. The result was that no one would respond to the buying and no one would accept the selling. Thus, the market was slow, the transaction turned to be less, and the market price did not rise or fall.

Securities Debt Market Storm Was Intense

The Result Was Still Flat, Each Bond Only Fell by Three to Four Jiao

Total Transactions Were 10,047,700 Yuan

Yesterday, a major change occurred in the situation of bonds on the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange. The loss of Chengde in Rehe and the increasingly serious situation in North China, coupled with the intensifying financial turmoil in the United States, caused the margin market in this port to be almost impossible to bid on, with private trading falling by more than 100 taels. The public debt market was also shocked, with the northern help selling No. 20 and No. 47 as soon as the market opened, and retail investors following suit. Although No. 11 and No. 38 and others still had a good appetite, the forces were too far apart, and the market price fell uniformly by about one yuan. The second round was still depressed, but at the same time, a certain giant account absorbed quite a bit, so the continued drop was only three or four jiao. The 19 Customs and salt tax futures even raised one jiao, and people's hearts suddenly became dazed. In the afternoon, the situation changed abruptly, and although many of No. 2 and No. 47 were sold, the market price could not be lowered. The market prices of each bond increased by several jiao. The 20 Customs even rose by one yuan, and the closing price of demobilization rose by nine jiao. The market price reversed so quickly, or it was said that because of the change in Rehe, it was feared that a drastic change would occur in the market, and a certain official maintained it from the middle. Speculators used the previous situation as a warning from the past, so the change of wind was also extremely fast, so there was an image of rabbits rising and falcons falling. At the moment, the most important thing is to hope that North China does not get caught in the whirlpool, otherwise the future of the market price is unimaginable. The result of yesterday's market price was still flat, with only a drop of three or four jiao, and demobilization only fell by five jiao, and reorganization rose by five fen. The total transaction volume was relatively large, totaling 10,047,400 yuan, of which spot trading accounted for four types, totaling 14,000 yuan, and futures salt tax made 1.57 million, and demobilization and unified tax each made 2.07 million, and the rest only made tens of thousands.

Flour and Wheat Markets: Morning Advance, Afternoon Retreat 246

| Price Differences Among Different Months Vary Greatly |

Flour Market 247

After trading began yesterday morning, the market for each month showed an initial rise followed by a decline. The quotation for foreign wheat, particularly Canadian wheat, rose by 50 cents, which caused people's sentiment to become briefly firm, with prices increasing by approximately 5 cents. However, in subsequent trading sessions, the market gradually weakened due to a rare drop in the gold market, which was expected to lead to a significant increase in exchange rates. Additionally, some factories followed the trend and sold off holdings, causing prices for various months to fall again, from 1.5 to 2 cents. When trading began in the afternoon, market sentiment was initially flat, but later improved because, although there were no large-scale disposals of spot goods, sales were very brisk. Therefore, various merchants opened higher prices, showing signs of improvement. Given the current situation, if there are no problems at sea, and with the sharp fall in the gold market and the rise in exchange rates, there is concern that sellers of foreign wheat will come in an endless stream. This also requires attention. As a result, the current month was 5 li better than the previous week, April remained unchanged, May was 5 li better, June and July were slightly better by 2.5 li, and August was slightly better by 5 li.

Wheat Market 248

When trading began in the morning, the market for each month showed signs of improvement. The near-term price of Canadian wheat rose by 50 cents, and due to the severity of the international situation, people's sentiment became optimistic. Prices for each month opened 2, 3, or 4 cents higher than the previous day. However, when trading began in the afternoon, near-term sentiment weakened again because the flour market had risen and then fallen in the morning, and the gold market had sharply declined while the exchange rate had risen. People inevitably became concerned. March and April fell back by 2 to 4 cents, but longer-dated months saw continued buying interest as selling interest was low, leading to a trend of market expansion. As a result, the current month remained unchanged, April fell slightly by 1 cent, July rose by 2 cents, and August rose by 4 cents.
